| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.

ed, 758 were to members of the out

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i

of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '

tor of Education, 2.

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.

which were conferred today is as
follows:

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.
The complete list of degrees
which were conferred today is as
follows:

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.
The complete list of degrees
which were conferred today is as
follows:

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.
The complete list of degrees
which were conferred today is as
follows:

i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.

ed, 758 were to members of the out

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.
The complete list of degrees
which were conferred today is as
follows:

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.

which were conferred today is as
follows:

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.
The complete list of degrees
which were conferred today is as
follows:

I P" ..LOWING a solemn procession into the Memorial Church this morn
| i"K. 1-130 candidates for degrees emerged two hours later carrying
| with them their diplomas. The best wishes of Stanford were extended
i to the departing Class of ';!() by Dr. Robert Eckles Swain, acting presi
} dent of the University, in his commencement address and in the message
| from President Wilbur which he read following his own address. The
| somber robes of the graduates contrasted sharply with the gayly colored

dresses of their guests as they
mingled in the Inner Quad receiv- i
ing the congratulations of friends I
and relatives.
Stanford's thirty-ninth class had '
gathered for the last time as mem
bers of the University community,!
and was exchanging final goodbyes
before scattering to Hie four cor
ners of Hie earth. Some are return
ing to the Orient, some to Europe,
others to South America: never
will they all be gathered In one
place again.
Of the number of degrees grant
ed, 758 were to members of the out
going senior class. The remaining
272 awarded were advanced de
grees. The degree of Master of Arts
was conferred on 1(>4; Juris Dflctor, i
52; Doctor of Medicine, 42; Doctor :
of Philosophy, 41; Engineer, 30; '
Master of Business Administration,
25; Bachelor of Laws, 1 (i; and Doc- i
tor of Education, 2.
The complete list of degrees
which were conferred today is as
follows:
